**GT numerical expression:** `-0.16498*A² - 0.16498*A*exp(-0.01276*t) + 0.6208*sin(log(A + 1))`

The GT has three distinct basis functions:
1. `A²` (polynomial in A)
2. `A*exp(-0.01276*t)` (product of A and decaying exponential in t)
3. `sin(log(A + 1))` (sine of logarithm of A+1)

The critical term is `sin(log(A+1))` — this is a very specific nonlinear function of A that cannot be replicated by polynomials, rational functions, logarithms, or simple powers of A.

Let me check each candidate for the presence of `sin(log(A+...))` or equivalent:

- Candidate 46: has `log(c2*|t|+1)` — log of t, not A
- Most candidates have combinations of: A², A, A*exp(t), exp(t), t*exp(t), log(A+1), A^c, rational functions of A, etc.

**Key question:** Can `sin(log(A+1))` be approximated or exactly matched by any of these basis functions?

No. `sin(log(A+1))` is an oscillatory function (though slowly oscillating for A>0) that is fundamentally different from:
- Polynomials in A
- Powers `A^c`
- Logarithms `log(A+1)`
- Rational functions of A
- Products of these with exponentials in t

By the principle of linear independence of basis functions, none of these can exactly equal `sin(log(A+1))` for all A ≥ 0.

Let me verify no candidate contains `sin(log(...))`:

Going through all 50 candidates — none contains `sin(log(A + c))` or any equivalent construction. The only trigonometric terms appear in:

None of these can produce `sin(log(A+1))`.
